## Interpolate hybrid/sigma -> pressure coordinates

Reference materials:

1. NCL method [vinth2p_ecmwf](https://www.ncl.ucar.edu/Document/Functions/Built-
in/vinth2p_ecmwf.shtml)

2. [Logarithmic interpolation in python
(Stackoverflow)](http://stackoverflow.com/questions/29346292/logarithmic-
interpolation-in-python)

3. [UV-CDAT loglinear interpolation method](https://github.com/UV-CDAT/uvcdat/bl
ob/e464caeaf8f91265ef49eb472d7fcace2bb751d4/Packages/cdutil/Lib/vertical.py)

```{.python .input  n=30}
import xray

data = xray.open_dataset("/Users/daniel/Desktop/MARC_AIE/F2000"
                           "/arg_comp/arg_comp.cam2.h0.0008-06.nc",
                           decode_times=False)
```

Reconstruct pressure field on sigma levels from the surface pressure

```{.python .input  n=31}
a, b = data['hyam'], data['hybm']
P0 = data['P0']
PS = data['PS']
pres_sigma = a*P0 + b*PS
# Copy attributes and overwrite where different
pres_sigma.attrs.update(PS.attrs)
pres_sigma.attrs['long_name'] = "Pressure field on sigma levels"

```
Choose some mandatory levels for reference.
```{.python .input  n=32}
import numpy as np
mandatory_levs = 100.*np.array([100., 250., 300., 500., 700., 
                                850., 925., 1000.])
```

Select some reference cloud data, and extract a 1D column.

```{.python .input  n=33}
A = data['CLOUD'].isel(lat=48, lon=72, time=0).squeeze()
P = pres_sigma.isel(lat=48, lon=72, time=0).squeeze()
```

Interpolate in log-linear space using scipy's toolkit, then re-project back into
original linear space.

```{.python .input  n=34}
from scipy.interpolate import interp1d

# Treat original function as mapping y = f(x),
# where y = the data being interpolated, and x is the sigma-pressure
# coordinates. Compute logs of these values
# logA = np.log10(A)
logA = A
logP = np.log10(P)

# Create interpolater. Need to disable bounds error checking so that
# it will automatically fill in missing values
lin_interp = interp1d(logP, logA, bounds_error=False)

# New coordinates (x'), mapped to log space
logP_new = np.log10(mandatory_levs)

# Compute interpolation on the new levels
interped_logA = lin_interp(logP_new)

# Re-project to linear space
# A_new = np.power(10., interped_logA)
A_new = interped_logA
```

As a sanity check, plot the interpolated values

```{.python .input  n=35}
%matplotlib inline
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import seaborn as sns
sns.set(style='ticks', context='talk')

plt.plot(A, P/100., '-k', marker='s',  lw=2, label="$\sigma$-P")
plt.plot(A_new, mandatory_levs/100., 'or', label='Interpolated')

plt.legend()
plt.ylim(plt.ylim()[-1], 100)
plt.semilogy()
```


---

Generalize to multiple dimensions

```{.python .input}
import marc_analysis as ma

A = data['CLOUD'].squeeze()
P = pres_sigma.squeeze()

# Shuffle dims so that 'lev' is first for simplicity
A = ma.shuffle_dims(A)
P = ma.shuffle_dims(P)

print(A.shape, P.shape, A.dims)

# Find the 'lev' axis for interpolating
axis = A.dims.index('lev')
nlev = A.shape[axis]

cols = int(np.product(A.shape)/nlev)

nlev_new = len(mandatory_levs)
A_new = np.zeros((nlev_new, cols))

temp_shape = (nlev, cols)
# logA = np.reshape(np.log10(A.data), temp_shape)
logA = np.reshape(A.data, temp_shape)
logP = np.reshape(np.log10(P.data), temp_shape)
```

```{.python .input}
from tqdm import *

for col in tqdm(range(cols)):
    
    # Create interpolater. Need to disable bounds error checking so that
    # it will automatically fill in missing values
    lin_interp = interp1d(logP[:, col], logA[:, col], axis=axis,
                          bounds_error=False, assume_sorted=True)

    # New coordinates (x'), mapped to log space
    logP_new = np.log10(mandatory_levs)

    # Compute interpolation on the new levels
    interped_logA = lin_interp(logP_new)
    A_new[:, col] = interped_logA

# A_new = np.power(10., A_new)
    
final_shape = tuple([nlev_new, ] + list(A.shape[1:]))
A_new = np.reshape(A_new, final_shape)
```

```{.python .input}
# Create new DataArray based on interpolated data
new_coords = {}
dims = []
for c in A.dims:
#     print(c, A.coords[c])
    if c == 'lev':
        new_coords[c] = mandatory_levs
    else:
        new_coords[c] = A.coords[c]
    dims.append(c)
A_new = xray.DataArray(A_new, coords=new_coords, dims=dims, )
```

```{.python .input}
import marc_analysis as ma
import marc_analysis.plot as mplt

A_plot = A_new.sel(lev=850*100)#.mean('time', keep_attrs=True)
levels = [0., 0.05, 0.1, 0.15, 0.2, 0.25, 0.3, 0.35, 
          0.4, 0.45, 0.5, 0.55, 0.6]

ax, cf = mplt.geo_plot(A_plot, levels=levels)
plt.colorbar(cf, ax=ax, orientation='horizontal')
plt.savefig("naive_interp.png")

A_ds = xray.Dataset({'CLOUD': A_new})
A_ds.to_netcdf("naive_interp.nc")
```

Clearly the naive way - iterating over every column - works ok, if not a little
bit slow (not prohibitively by any means).

However, it might be nicer if we can take advantage of `xray` dimension
broadcasting and implement a method like that of UV-CDAT which handles all the
grid cells as the same time.

```{.python .input}
import marc_analysis as ma

A = data['CLOUD'].squeeze()
P = pres_sigma.squeeze()

# Shuffle dims so that 'lev' is first for simplicity
A = ma.shuffle_dims(A)
P = ma.shuffle_dims(P)

print(A.shape, P.shape, A.dims)

# Find the 'lev' axis for interpolating
axis = A.dims.index('lev')
nlev = A.shape[axis]

nlev_new = len(mandatory_levs)
A_interp_shape = [nlev_new, ] + list(A.shape[1:])
A_new = np.zeros(A_interp_shape)
```

Re-implement method from UV-CDAT - https://github.com/UV-CDAT/uvcdat/blob/e464ca
eaf8f91265ef49eb472d7fcace2bb751d4/Packages/cdutil/Lib/vertical.py

```{.python .input}
# Shape of array at any given level
flat_shape = P.isel(lev=0).shape

n_sigma = nlev # Number of original sigma levels
n_interp = len(mandatory_levs) # Number of interpolant levels

# Loop over the interpolant levels
for ilev in range(n_interp):
    
    lev = mandatory_levs[ilev]
#     if lev != 850.*100: continue
    
    P_abv = np.ones(flat_shape)
    # Array on sigma level above, below
    A_abv, A_bel = -1.*P_abv, -1.*P_abv
    # Pressure on sigma level above, below
    P_abv, P_bel = -1.*P_abv, -1.*P_abv
    
    # Mask area where pressure == levels
    P_eq = np.ma.masked_equal(P_abv, -1)
    
    # Loop from the second sigma level to the last one
    for i in tqdm(range(1, n_sigma)):
        a = np.ma.greater_equal(P.isel(lev=i),   lev) # sigma-P > lev?
        b =    np.ma.less_equal(P.isel(lev=i-1), lev) # sigma-P < lev?
        
        # Now, if the interpolant level is between the two 
        # sigma levels, then we can use these two levels for the
        # interpolation.
        a = (a & b)

        # Pressure on sigma level above, below
#         P_abv[a], P_bel[a] = P[i].data[a], P[i-1].data[a]
        P_abv = np.where(a, P[i], P_abv)
        P_bel = np.where(a, P[i-1], P_bel)
#         Array on sigma level above, below
#         A_abv[a], A_bel[a] = A[i].data[a], A[i-1].data[a]
        A_abv = np.where(a, A[i], A_abv)
        A_bel = np.where(a, A[i-1], A_bel)

#         sel = P[i] == lev
#         P_eq[sel] = A[i].data[sel]
        P_eq = np.where(P[i] == lev, A[i], P_eq)
        
    # If no data below, set to missing value; if there is, set to 
    # (interpolating) level
    P_val = np.ma.masked_where((P_bel == -1), np.ones_like(P_bel)*lev)
    
    # Calculate interpolation
    tl = np.log(P_val/P_bel)/np.log(P_abv/P_bel)*(A_abv - A_bel) + A_bel
    tl.fill_value = np.nan
    
    # Copy into result array, masking where values are missing
    # because of bad interpolation (out of bounds, etc.)
    tl[tl.mask] = np.nan
    A_new[ilev] = tl
```

```{.python .input}
# Create new DataArray based on interpolated data
new_coords = {}
dims = []
for c in A.dims:
#     print(c, A.coords[c])
    if c == 'lev':
        new_coords[c] = mandatory_levs
    else:
        new_coords[c] = A.coords[c]
    dims.append(c)
A_new = xray.DataArray(A_new, coords=new_coords, dims=dims, )
```

```{.python .input}
import marc_analysis as ma
import marc_analysis.plot as mplt

A_plot = A_new.sel(lev=850*100)#.mean('time', keep_attrs=True)
# A_plot.data[A_plot.data >= 1] = np.nan
levels = [0., 0.05, 0.1, 0.15, 0.2, 0.25, 0.3, 0.35, 
          0.4, 0.45, 0.5, 0.55, 0.6]

ax, cf = mplt.geo_plot(A_plot, levels=levels)
plt.colorbar(cf, ax=ax, orientation='horizontal')
plt.savefig("uvcdat_interp.png")

A_ds = xray.Dataset({'CLOUD': A_new})
A_ds.to_netcdf("uvcdat_interp.nc")
```

---

Finally, test the implementation in the `marc_analysis` package.

```{.python .input  n=6}
from marc_analysis.analysis import interp_to_pres_levels

A = data['CLOUD']
P = pres_sigma
A_scipy = interp_to_pres_levels(A, P, [50000., 85000.], method='scipy')
A_numpy = interp_to_pres_levels(A, P, [50000., 85000.], method='numpy')
```

```{.python .input  n=24}
import marc_analysis.plot as mplt

%matplotlib inline

As_plot = A_scipy.sel(lev=850*100)
An_plot = A_numpy.sel(lev=850*100)
levels = [0., 0.05, 0.1, 0.15, 0.2, 0.25, 0.3, 0.35, 
          0.4, 0.45, 0.5, 0.55, 0.6]

proj = mplt.get_projection("Robinson")
fig, axes = mplt.multipanel_figure(2, 1, aspect=16./10.,
                                   cbar_orientation='vertical',
                                   projection=proj)
axes = list(axes.ravel())

ax1, cf1 = mplt.geo_plot(As_plot, levels=levels, ax=axes[0])
ax2, cf2 = mplt.geo_plot(An_plot, levels=levels, ax=axes[1])

cb = mplt.add_colorbar(cf2, fig=fig, orientation='vertical', 
                       shrink=0.01)
```
